PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Transmitting a Com munication, dated August 8, 2001 from
JOH N H. STROG ER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners

I am hereby forwarding for your consideration an Ordinance authorizing an agreement with the Boeing
Company to provide for real estate tax reimbursement as an incentive to corporate relocation as
authorized by the Illinois Corporate Headquarters Relocation Act (PA 92-0207), sig ned into law on
Aug ust I , 200 I.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

AN ORDINANCE OF THE COUNTY OF COOK, ILLINOIS
APPROVING EXECUTION OF A
TAX REIMBURSEMENT PAYMENT AGREEMENT
WITH THE BOEING COMPANY
WHERE AS, pursuant to the Corporate Headquarters Relocati on Act, (PA 92-0207), signed into
law on August I , 2001 , as amended from time to time (the " Relocati on Act"), the General Assembly of
the State of Illinois (the "State") has detennined that the relocation of the international headquarters of
large, multinational corporations from outside of the State to a location within the State creates a
substantial public benefit and wi ll foster economic growth and development; and
WHEREAS, the Re location Act therefore provides for the creatio n of certain financial
incentives that may be used to encourage long-term commitments by an Eligible Business relocating its
Corporate Headquarters (as such terms are defined in the Re location Act) in the State; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook (the "County"), as an affected taxing district, is authorized
under the provisions of Section 18 of the Property Tax Code, 35 ILCS 200/1 et seq., as amended from
time to time (the "Property Tax Code "), to, by a majority vote of its governing body, after the
determination of the assessed valuation of its property, to order the C lerk of Cook County to abate any
po rti on of its taxes on certa in types of real property. Pursuant to Section I 8- l 65(a)(8) of the Property
Tax Code, 35 ILCS 200/l 8- J65(a)(8), s uch abatement may be made with respect to any property or a
po rtion of any property within the County that is used by an Eligible Bus iness for a Corporate
Headquarters. Alternatively, in lie u of such abatement, the County may enter into an agreement with an
Eligible Business to make annual payments to such Eligible Business in an amo unt no t to exceed the
property taxes paid directly o r indirectly by such Eligible Business to the taxing district and any other

25 11

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
affected taxing district(s) for premises occupied pursuant to a written lease and may make such payments
without the need for an annual appropriation. Any such abatement or agreement may be effective for the
entire term specified by the County, provided, however, that such abatement or annual payments in lieu
thereof may not exceed 20 years; and

WHEREAS, the Boeing Company (" Boeing") is a large, multinational corporation with worldwide revenues in excess of $50,000,000,000 that presently maintains its international headquarters in
Seattle, Washington. Boeing intends to relocate its international headquarters to the real property
commonly known as I 00 N. Riverside Plaza, Chicago, Jllinois 60606 (the " Property"). In connection with
such relocation, Boeing has executed that certain Office Lease dated May I 0, 200 I by and between I 00
North Riverside, LLC, as landlord, and Boeing, as tenant (the " Boeing Lease"), pursuant to which Boeing
shall, among other matters, initially lease approximately 275,000 rentable square feet of space including
the top 12 floors of the building located on the Property (the " Building") for an initial period of fifteen
(15) years, subject to the terms and conditions contained therein. Upon such relocation, and during the
Term of the Agreement, as defined in the Tax Reimbursement Payment Agreement (the " Agreement")
submitted hereto as Exhibit A, the portion of the Building occupied by Boeing will be the principal office
of Boeing and the site which Boeing's principal executive officers have designated as their principal
offices. In connection with its occupancy of the Building, Boeing shall construct substantial tenant
improvements necessary to permit Boeing to take possession in accordance with the terms of the Boeing
Lease. Such relocation will create a substantial public benefit through its creation of not less than 500
permanent FTE jobs (as defined in the Agreement), through Boeing' s payment of various taxes and
governmental charges and through other public benefits described in this Agreement and wi ll also foster
further economic growth and development in the County and State. Therefore, Boeing constitutes an
Eligible Business under the Relocation Act and the portion of the Building occupied by Boeing will, upon
such occupancy, constitute Boeing's new Corporate Headquarters; and
WHEREAS, the County' s annual reimbursement payments under the Agreement wil l consist of
the County's allocable share of the Boeing General Real Estate Taxes (as defined in the Agreement), the
Forest Preserve District of Cook County a llocable share of the Boeing General Real Estates Taxes, based
on the respective tax rates of such taxing district(s) or fund ; and
WHEREAS, the County's agreement to provide the annual reimbursement payments provided
for in the Agreement is conditioned upon, among other things, (i) Boeing's relocation to the Building, as
described above, (ii) Boeing's construction of certain initial Boeing improvements, (iii) Boeing's
continued status during the Term of the Agreement as an Eligible Business under the Relocation Act, (iv)
the continued status of the portion of the Building occupied by Boeing as a Corporate Headquarters under
the Relocation Act during the Term of the Agreement, (v) Boeing's relocation to and retention at the
Building of not less than the minimum number of FTE jobs and the corporate headquarters employees
specified in the Agreement during the Term of the Agreement, (vi) Boeing's lease and occupancy of not
less than the mi nimum number of square feet at the Building specified in the Agreement during the Term
of the Agreement, and (vii) Boeing's compliance with the job readiness training and public benefit
requirements specified in the Agreement, all subject to the terms and conditions set forth in the
Agreement; and
WHEREAS, Boeing' s relocation to the County would not reasonably be anticipated without the
payment of the annual reimbursement payments provided for in the Agreement and the comparable
agreements being executed and delivered by the other taxing districts levying property taxes on the
Property and the Building; now therefore,

2512

 JOURNA L OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONE RS OF COOK COUNTY:
SECTION 1. The President of the Board of Commissioners authorized, negotiate, execute and
deli ver the Agreement between the County and Boeing substantially in the form submitted hereto as
Exhibit A and made a part he reof, and such other supporting documents as may be necessary to carry out
and comply with the provisions of the Agreement, with such changes, deletions and insertions as shall be
approved by the persons executing such agreement.
SECTION 2. The annual re imbursement payments required to be made by the County pursuant
to the Agreement may be made without annual appropriation, as provided for under Section 18-165(a)(8)
of the Property Tax Code, 35 ILCS 200/ I 8- I65(a)(8), as the same may be amended.
SEC TION 3. The President and County Clerk are a uthorized to execute and deliver on behalf of
the C ity such other documents, agreements and certificates and to do s uch other things consistent with the
terms of this Ordinance as s uch officers and employees s ha ll deem necessary or appropriate in order to
effectuate the intent and purposes of this Ordinance.
SECTION 4. If any provision of this Ordinance s ha ll be held to be invalid or unenforceable fo r
any reason, the invalidity or unenforceability of such provision shall not affect any of the other provisions
of this Ordinance.
SECTION 5. All ord inances, resolutions, motions or orders in conflict with this Ordinance are
hereby repealed to the extent of such conflict.
SECTION 6. This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect immediately upon its passage.

Commi ssioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to suspend the ru les so that
this matter may be considered. T he motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be re ferred
to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 245585). T he motion carried unanimously.

PETER N. SIL VESTRJ, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CA RR,

PROPOSED SUBSTITUTE ORDINANCE
COOK COUNTY AMUSEMENT NOTIFICATION PROCEDURE
WHEREAS, the National Institute on Drug Abuse reports that the use of Ecstasy and other "club
drugs" is on the rise and continues to spread in both urban an suburban populations, unlike the use of
other illicit drugs, which are stabilizing or in the decline; and
WHEREAS, National Institute on Drug Abuse supported research has shown that use of club
drugs can cause serious, long-lasting health problems and even death, and that used in combination with
alcohol, these drugs become more dangerous; and

25 15

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS, because some club drugs can be added unobtrusively to beverages by individuals
who want to intoxicate or sedate others, there has been an increase in reports of club drugs used to
commit sexual assaults; and
WHEREAS, many of these clubs are allowed to stay open until 4:00 a.m. on weekends and have
a section in which adults can purchase alcohol; and
WHEREAS, teens gravitate to juice bars and teen dance clubs to dance to electronic music; and
WHEREAS, Ecstasy is commonly used in juice bars and teen dance clubs to enhance the
dancing experience; and
WHEREAS, Ecstasy raises the body temperature and when taken in a hot atmosphere the
physical and psychological risks associated with its use increase, which has resulted in a jump in
emergency room visits by teens frequentingjuice bars and teen dance clubs; and
WHEREAS, in the past year, Cook County Sheriffs Police have made more than I 00 arrests in
undercover Ecstasy investigations in unincorporated Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
("Board") amend the Cook County Code of Ordinances to include the following:
DANCE HALL AND ROADHOUSES
Lieense Notification Required
No citizen, firm or corporation of this state shall operate a public dance hall 0f
14-31.
roadhouse used for public youth dances in the county and outside the limits of any city, town or village,
without first haviAg obtaiAed a eouAt)' roadhouse lieeAse for eaeh loeatioA of aA)' roadhouse or daAee hall
except under the following conditions.
Any public establishment used or intended to be used for participation by minors in
14-31.1
entertainment or amusement, involving music, music videos or dancing (examples include, but are not
limited to: a dry dance hall, non-alcohol bar, teenage cabaret or juice bar) shall not operate between the
hours of 12:00 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. and shall not be eligible for a retail liquor license under Chapter 14 of
the Cook County Code of Ordinances.
14-31.2
For purposes of this ordinance: "Amusement" means any exhibition, performance,
presentation or show for entertainment purposes, including, but not limited to, those involving music,
music videos or dancing.
14-31.3
It s hall be unlawful for any person who owns, maintains or manages an establishment
for participation by youth in such activities to operate without providing written notice to, the Cook
County Sheriffs Police.
14-31.4
If an amusement is produced, presented or conducted for gain of profit on any
property in unincorporated Cook County without proper notice to the Cook County Sheriffs Police, all of
the following persons shall be found in violation: I) the owner of the property if it is established that the
owner knew or should have known that such operation occurred without proper notice as evidenced by
failing to secure a copy of such notice from the lessee to the Sheriff; 2) the lessee of the property; 3) the
manager of the property; 4) the producer of the amusement; 5) the presenter of the amusement; and 6) the
person conducting the amusement. Each person found in violation of this s ubsection shall be subject to a
fine of up to $1,500.00.

2516

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 200 I
14-31.5
It shall be unlawful for any person who owns, maintains or manages an establishment
allowing such an amusement to rent, lease or make the establishment avai lable for use, with or without
compensation, for the purpose of unlawfully manufacturing, storing, distributing or using a controlled
substance.

a) For purpose of this section, the term "controlled substance" shall be defined in the Illinois
Controlled Substances Act, codified at 720 ILCS 570/ 100 et seq., as amended.
b) Any person who violates this subsection shall be sentenced to a term of imprisonment of not
less than 30 days nor more than 6 months in the Cook County Department of Corrections, and
a fine of up to $ 1,500.00.
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED that the Cook County Sheriffs Office shall develop a notice procedure
for obtaining authority to operate such an establishment no later than December I, 200 I.

The Ordinance shall become effective on December I, 200 I.

Commissioner Silvestri , seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved that the Proposed Substitute
Ordinance be referred to the Committee on Law Enforcement and Corrections. (Com m. No. 245582).
The motion carried unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESO LUTION
WHEREAS, Cook County makes a substantial investment in terms of time and money in providing for
the training of newly hired employees for the Sheriffs Office; and
WHEREAS, the Sheriff is entitled to expect a reasonable return on such investment, in terms of the
commitment and devotion to duty of their prospective employees; and
WHEREAS, it has become prevalent for employees to leave the Sheriff' s Office and the community,

which provided their training and equipment before a reasonable amount of time has passed.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED
COMMISSIONERS AS FOLLOWS:

BY

THE

COOK

COUNTY

Section l - Title

This Resolution shall be known as the Cook County Training Reimbursement Agreement.

25 17

BOARD

OF

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001

Section 2 - Scope
This Resolution applies to all non-civilian employees of the Sheriff's Office who receive equipment
and/or training for their position with the Sheriff's Office, including but not limited to Deputy Sheriff's,
Correction 's Officers, Court Services Officers and Community Services Officers.

Section 3 -Agreement
I.

The Cook County Sheriff's Employee within the scope of this Resolution ("Employee") agrees to
participate in the Sheriff' s required law enforcement training. The Employee further agrees to
successfully complete such training and obtain the necessary and appropriate certification. The
Employee then agrees to serve as an Employee of the Cook County Sheriff's Office. Said
Employee does further agree to devote full-time to the traini ng and subsequent service and to
perform all assignments in a satisfactory manner.

2.

The Sheriff agrees to make available to the Employee law enforcement training as set forth
above, and to be responsible for and to pay for all related expenses in connection therewith,
including equipment and salaries on the premises while the Employee is in training, if required,
and further, to provide in-house training for the Employee during the periods of time that said
Em ployee is employed with the Sheriff's Office, but not attending the training academy.

3.

The cost and expenses related to the training and equipping of the Employee change with time
along with any increase in expenses, changing the cost of a breach of this Agreement by the
Employee. Any Employee found to have violated this agreement agrees to pay the County the
sum of:
The cost of training the Employee for the current year, when that Employee has less than twelve
( 12) months of service to the Sheriffs Office.
The Employee shall pay this amount not as penalty, but as agreed upon liquidated damages, in the
event that said Employee terminates said employment with the Sheriff during training withi n the
first twelve ( 12) months subsequent to taking the oath of office.

4.

In no event shall liquidated damages, as set forth above, be assessed if the Employee fail s to
sati sfactorily complete the training, or terminates his or her employment during the first twel ve
( 12) months, due to disabling illness or injury, verified by a physician of the Sheriff' s choice.

5.

The exceptions as set forth in paragraph four (4) above shall not apply in the event that there is
substantial evidence that the Employee has been dismissed as a resu lt of misrepresenting hi s or
her basic qualifications for employment, or has caused his or her dismissal , failure, illness or
injury in an attempt to avoid payment of liquidated damages set forth above.

6.

Damages assessed herein wi ll be prorated according to the amount of training completed, in the
event said damages should become payable prior to the Employee taking the oath of office after
the completion of the training period required by the Sheriff's Office.

7.

Said Employee acknowledged that he or she meets the basic qualifications for employment as set
forth by the Sheriff.

2518

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
8.

Said Employee also states that the information placed on his or her formal application and that
given to personnel conducting any background investigation is accurate and complete to the best
of his or her knowledge.

9.

In the event that the Employee is called to active military duty, or has his or her probationary
period extended for any reason whatsoever, or is granted a leave of absence during any period of
time contemplated by this Agreement, the period of said Agreement shall be extended
accordingly.

10.

This Agreement shall become effective upon Employee's official starting date and shall remain in
fu ll force and effect for twelve ( 12) months following admini stration of the oath of office, unless
extended as provi ded in paragraph nine (9) above.

11 .

This Agreement is to be construed in accordance with the laws of the State of Illinois, and
embodies the entire agreement between the parties hereto, and each party acknowledges that there
are no inducements, promises, terms, conditions or obligations made or entered into other than
those contained herein.

12.

This Resolution shall take effect for all Employees hired by the Sheriffs Office after the approval
of this Resolution by the Cook County Board of Commissioners.

Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 245583). The motion carried unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, mass transit is most important to individuals who can not provide their own transportation;
and
WHEREAS, Pace and many other transportation organizations are trying to control s pending in order to
lower their spending in order to pay the increase costs of fuel; and
WHEREAS, one proposal involves eliminating bus routes and other services in order to save money; and
WHEREAS, eliminati ng routes wi ll leave some individuals w ith no transportation to and from their jobs;
and
WHEREAS, in several meetings regarding changes in routes the people affected have pleaded for the
route to continue and even offered to pay increased fares to increase the fund s of the transportation
provider; and
WHEREAS, Pace is considering the eli mination of a route they have provided for individuals working at
the LARC (Lansing Association of Retarded Citizens) facility in Lansing, Illinois; and

2519

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS, by eliminating this service Pace has provided for LARC, the families of the individuals
going there,and many of the individuals will have no other way to go to the LARC facility in order to
work; and
WHEREAS, the United States Department of Transportation regulations require transportation providers
to transport qualified individuals under the Americans with Disabilities Act within 3/.i to I Y2 a mile of
transportation routes, leaving some Americans with no transportation options if they go beyond this
covered area; and
WHEREAS, the State of Illinois requires downstate transportation authorities to maintain a profit of
twelve percent, yet Chicago area transportation providers must maintain a forty percent profit, creating a
greater financial burden on Cook County residents and transportation providers; and
WHEREAS, all the levels of government and the transportation providers should work together in order
to assure that those who most need mass transit are able to get to and from their destinations.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners encourages
Pace to continue to transport qualified individuals under the Americans with Disability Act, and others
who can not transport themselves, to and from their destinations in and around Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that transportation providers should pay special attention to areas
which contain people unable to provide their own transportation when creating, maintaining, altering or
discontinuing any transportation routes; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby encourage
the Federal and State of Illinois Governments to examine the transportation issues mentioned within this
Resolution, especially services for qualified individuals under the Americans with Disabilities Act and the
amount of profit required for transportation providers.

Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Legislation and Intergovernmental Relations. (Comm. No. 245584). The
motion carried unanimously.

DONALD H. WLODARSKl, Commissioner, Department of Building and Zoning
respectfully requests the granting of a 10% No Fee Permit for Loyola University Medical Center for the
New Ambulatory Care Center at 2 160 South First Avenue, Maywood, Ill inois in Proviso Township.
Permit#:

Requested Waived Fee Amount (90%):

This request is pursuant to the County Board's adoption of Item No. 176427 on September 16, 1991 that
valid not-for-profit organizations be required to pay ten percent ( 10%) of the standard permit fees as
established by Ordinance.

Transmitting a Communication from
DOROTHY BROWN , Clerk of the Circuit Court
requesting authori zation for the Purchasing Age nt to enter into a contract with Cristo Rey Work/Study
Program, Inc. , Chicago, Illinois, not-for-profit corporation, to provide four (4) work/study students
equaling approximately one full-time position for the 2001-2002 school year.
Reason:

Cristo Rey Work/Study Program, Inc. serves a mostly Latino, low-income community in the
Pilsen/Little Village neighborhood. The students who attend Cristo Rey Jesuit High School
earn the bulk of their tuition through the Work/Study Program serving as interns in various
corporations and organizations. Each student on the team attends five days of work at a
Chicago-area business each month. C lass and work schedules are designed so that students
are never required to miss one for the other. The program provides an innovative means of
providing students with crucial hands-on work experience while simultaneously enabling
them to finance a portion of their education. As a result of working in a business
environment, students acquire desirable job experience and marketable skills, develop a
network of business contacts, gain exposure to a wide variety of career opportunities, develop
a strong work ethic, and increase their self esteem.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $25,000.00. Contract period: August I, 200 I through July 31 , 2002. (360-260
Account). Requisition No. 13600705.

Commi ssioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

BUREAU OF HEALTH SERVICES
COOPERATIVE EDUCATIONAL MASTER AGREEMENT PROGRAM ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 25, 200 I from
RUTH M. ROTHSTEIN, Chief, Bureau of Health Services
requesting authorization from the Cook County Board of Commissioners to extend by twelve ( 12) months
and amend the scope of the agreement with the Board of Trustees of Community College District No.
508, Chicago, Illinois, to provide monies for scholarship and book funds. This allocation will provide
relief for deserving Malcolm X Physician Assistant Students who as adult learners are not eligible for
standard student aid.
For over ten years Cook County Hospital and Malcolm X College have jointly sponsored the Physician
Assistant Student Program whose mission is to prepare individuals to become certified physician
assistants and to practice in medically underserved communities. Since the program requires two full
years of intensive study and significant clinical experience at Cook County Hospital, these funds were
requested to enable needy students to complete the course of study. Eligi bility for the award of fund s will
be based on financial need and service commitment. These funds will be disbursed to students selected
by a committee with Hospital representation.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $100,000.00. Contract period: August I, 200 I through July 31 , 2002. (899298 Account). Requisition No. 18990944.

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 15, 200 I from
WALLY S. KOS, P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Tiered Approach to Corrective Action Objectives Agreement
Amoco Oil Company
2405 West Augusta Boulevard (CH 822)
in the C ity of Chicago
Fiscal Impact: None

2564

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 200 I

01-R-518
RESOLUTION
This Agreement is entered into this 9th day of August 2001 pursuant to 35 Ill. Admin. Code
Section 742. I 020 by and between Amoco Oil Company as owner or operator of underground storage
tank(s) ("Owner/Operator") and the County of Cook, Illinois ("the County") as follows:
WHEREAS, Owner/Operator has owned and operated or currently owns a nd operates certain
undergro und fuel storage tanks which either are currently or were previously located at 2405 West
Augusta Boulevard in Chicago, Cook County, Illinois (hereinafter "the Site");
WHEREAS, the Illinois Emergency Management Agency ("!EMA") has confirmed a release of
contaminants in the soil and groundwater at the Site and the right of way adjacent to the boundary of the
Site. The !EMA has assigned incident number 923151 to this release at the Site. Submitted as Exhibit A
is a site map which shows the area of estimated contaminant impacted soil and/or groundwater at the time
of this Agreement in the right of way above Tier I residential levels under 35 Ill. Adm in. Code Part 742.
Also submitted as Exhibit B is a table showing the concentration of contaminants of concern, hereafter
"Contaminants", in soil and/or ground water within the area described in Exhibit A and which shows the
app licabl e Tier I objectives for soil and groundwater of the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency
(" !EPA") which are exceeded. The right of ways described in Exhibit A (commonly described as
Augusta Boulevard and Western Avenue and hereinafter described as the "Right-of Way"), adjacent to
the site is s ubject to this Agreement. As the drawings in the Exhibits are not plats, the boundary of the
Right-of-Way in the Exhibits may be an approximation of the actual Right-of-Way lines. The Right-ofWay is impractical to sample for Contaminants, however, the parties believe that the area of the Right-ofWay is adequate to encompass soil and/or groundwater within the Right-of-Way possibly impacted with
Contaminants from a release at the Site;
WHEREAS, Owner/Operator is pursuing a corrective action of the Site and of the Right-of-Way
adjacent to the boundary of the Site and intends to request risk-based, site specific soil and/or
groundwater remediation objectives from the IEPA under 35 Ill. Admin. Code Part 742. Under these
rules, use of risk-based, site specific remediation objectives in the Right-of-Way may require the use of a
Highway Authority Agreement as defined in 35 Ill. Adm in. Code Section 742. l 020;
WHEREAS, the County holds a fee simple interest or a dedication for highway purposes in the
Right-of-Way, and has jurisd iction over it. As such, the County exercises sole control over the access to
the soil and use of the groundwater beneath the Right-of-Way;
WHEREAS, the Owner/Operator and the County are desirous of preventing the use of
groundwater under the Right-of-Way as a potable or domestic s upply of water and to limit access as
described herein to the soil under the Right-of-Way that is contaminated from the release at level s above
residential Tier I remediation objectives;
WHEREAS, this Agreement is intended as a "Highway Authority Agreement" pursuant to the
terms of 35 Ill. Adm in. Code Section 742. 1020, which restricts the use of the land under the Right-ofWay adjacent to the Site.
1.

INCORPORATION OF RECJT ALS
The recitals set forth above are incorporated by reference as iffully set forth herein.

2565

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDfNGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001

2.

TERM AND REQUISITES FOR VALIDITY

(a) This Agreement shall commence upon the date the Cook County Board of Commissioners
authorizes its execution and shall continue until the Right-of-Way is demonstrated to be suitable for
unrestricted land use and there is no longer a need for this Agreement as a Highway Authority Agreement
and the IEPA has, upon written request to the IEPA by the Owner/Operator and notice to the County,
amended the notice in the chain of tile of the Site to reflect unencumbered fu ture use of the Right-of-Way.
(b) The IEPA must review and approve this Agreement. Upon the IEPA's approval of this
Agreement and issuance of a "No Further Remediation " letter ("NFR"), the Owner/Operator shall record
the NFR letter at its expense at the Cook County Recorder's Office in the chain of title for the Site. This
Agreement sha ll be referenced in the Illinois EPA's NFR fo r the Site. The reference shall direct inqui ries
to Cook County Bureau of Admini stration, Department of Highways, Attention: Superintendent, 69 West
Washington Street, 23rd Floor, Chicago, Illinois 60602, tel. (3 12) 603-1 600 fo r further information
regarding this Agreement.
(c) This Agreement shall be null and void as a Highway Authority Agreement if:
( I ) The IEPA does not approve it, or;
(2) Owner/Operator does not record the NFR letter.
The occurrence of either of the above conditions shall not void thi s Agreement as a land use
Agreement between Owner/Operator and the County.

3.

RIGHTS, DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES OF THE PARTIES

A.

The County

( I)
The County will prohibit the use of groundwater beneath the Right-of-Way that is contaminated
from the release at levels above Tier I residential remediation objectives as a potable or other domestic
supply of water and will limit access to soil under the Right-of-Way that is contaminated from the release
at levels above Tier I residential remediation objectives.
The County has the right to construct, reconstruct, improve, repair, maintain and operate a
(2)
highway upon its property or to a llow others to use the Right-of-Way by permit. The County reserves the
right and the right of those using its property under permit to remove contaminated soil or groundwater
above Tier I residential remediation objectives from its Ri ght-of-Way and to dispose of the same as
deemed appropriate not inconsistent with applicable environmental regulations so as to avoid causing a
further release of contaminants and to protect human health and the environment.
Prior to taking any such action, the County w ill first give Owner/Operator thirty (30) days written
notice, unless there is an immediate threat to the health or safety of the public or any individual, that it
intends to perform a site investigation in the Right-of-Way and remove or dispose of contaminated soil or
groundwater to the extent necessary fo r its work. The removal or disposal shall be based upon the site
investigation and any modificati ons thereto as field conditions dictate.
If the County deems it practicable, it may request Owner/Operator to review or perform the site
investigation and/or to remove and dispose of the contaminated soil and/or groundwater necessary for the
County's work in advance of that work. Failure of the County to give notice to Owner/Operator of its
intent to perfo rm a site investigation shall not constitute a violation of this Agreement.

2566

 JOURNA L OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
(3)
The County's sole responsibility under this Agreement with respect to others using the Ri ght-ofWay under permit from the County is to make an effort to notify its current permit holders of the
fo llowing and to include the fo llowing, or substantial ly similar, language in future standard permit
provisions in accordance with all environmental laws:
"As a condition of this permit, the permittee sha ll request the office issuing the pennit to identify
sites in the Right-of-Way where access to contaminated soil or gro undwater is governed by
Tiered Approach to Correcti ve Action Obj ectives Agreements. The permittee shall take
measures before, during and after any access to these sites to protect worker safety and human
health and the environment. Excavated, contaminated soil should be managed off-site in
accordance with all appl icable environmental laws and regulations."

B.

Owner/Operator

( I)
Owner/Operator agrees to reimburse the County for the reasonable costs it has incurred for or
will incur in the future in protecting human health and the environment, including, but not limited to,
investigating, identi fy ing, handling, storing and disposing of contaminated soil and groundwater in the
Ri ght-of-Way as a result of the release of contaminants at this S ite. There is a rebuttable presumption that
contaminants found in the Right-of-Way arose from a release form the Site. Owner/Operator's
reimbursement to the County under this paragraph shall be limited to ten thousand ($ 10,000.00) doll ars in
the event that the county has not given notice to Owner/Operator and it is determined that there was not
immediate threat to the health and safety of the public or any person.
(2)
As the pavement in the Right-of-Way may be considered an engineered barrier as defined in 35
Ill. Admin. Code, Subpart B, Section 742.200, Owner/Operator agrees to reimburse the County for: (a)
maintenance activities requested by Owner/Operator or (b) maintenance acti vities performed by the
County on the Right-of-Way in order to assure its physical integrity as an engineered barrier.
Owner/Operator shall not be obligated to reimburse the Coun ty for ordinance mainte nance consistent with
that performed by the Department on other County Highways; provided, however, that Owner/Operator,
purs uant to Paragraph 3(A)(2) and 3(8)( 1) herein, sha ll reimburse the County fo r any and all costs it
incurs in removing and disposing of any contam inants discovered within the Ri ght-of-Way, as required
by appl icable environmental laws, in the course of performing highway activities other than ordinary
maintenance. Owner/Operator understands that the County does not represent that it will perfo rm
maintenance on the Right-of-Way, or that it w ill mainta in the Right-of-Way as an engineered barrier, or
that the Right-of-Way will a lways re main a highway.
Owner/Operator agrees to indemnify and hold the County and its Commissioners, officers,
(3)
agents, director, employees, contractors, consultants and affi liates, permit holders, as well as any other
highway a uthorities maintaining the Right-of-Way pursuant to an agreement with the County harmless
from and against any and a ll liability, losses, claims, costs, damages, demand, penalties, or other expenses
(includ ing attorney's fees and other legal expenses occasioned by any real and potential claim, demand or
action (whether or not meritorious) associated with the release of contaminants from the Site, or which
arise(s) out of any of the rights granted or performance rendered by the County to Owner/Operator under
this Agreement, or pertaining to any representation made by the County under this Agreement.
Owner/Operator s hall promptly re imburse the County, on demand, fo r any and a ll liabilities made or
incurred by the indemnified parities to which this indemnity applies.
Owner/Operator agrees that it wi ll inform its personnel, if any, at the Site about this Agreement
(4)
and that s uch personnel shall notify anyone excavating in the Right-of-Way about this Agreement.

2567

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
(5)
Upon approval of this Agreement by the IEPA, Owner/Operator shall furnish to the County a
copy of the NFR letter along with proof that it has been recorded.

4.

BREACH

A.

By Owner/Operator

Should Owner/Operator, or its successors and/or assigns, violate any of the tenns of this
Agreement shall be null and void as a highway authority agreement at the County's option upon thirty
(30) days' written notice by the County. If the violation relates to Owner/Operator's failure to reimburse
the County, as provided in paragraphs 2(B)( I), (2) or (3), above, Owner/Operator may remedy the breach
by making payment within twenty (20) working days from the date the notice is received.

B.

By County

Violation of the terms of this Agreement by the County shall not void this Agreement unless the
IEPA has determined that the violation is grounds for voidance of this Agreement as a highway authority
agreement and the County has not cured the violation within such time as the !EPA has granted.
Should the County breach this, breach of Agreement, Owner/Operator's sole remedy is an action
for damages in the Illinois Court of Claims. Any and all claims for damages against the County arising at
any time for a breach of paragraph 2(A)( I) of this Agreement are limited to an aggregate maximum of
twenty thousand ($20,000.00) dollars. No other breach by the County of a provision in this Agreement is
actionable in Jaw or equity by Owner/Operator.
However, should the County convey, vacate or transfer jurisdiction of the Ri ght-of Way to an
entity other than a County agency, Owner/Operator may pursue an action under thi s Agreement against
such successor(s) in interest in a Court of Law.

5.

MISCELLANEOUS

A.
Binding Effect: This Agreement shall be binding upon and inure to the benefit of the successors
and assigns of Owner/Operator in the Site and the County in the Right-of-Way as if they too were parties
to this Agreement.
B.
Severability: This Agreement is entered into by the County in recognition of laws passed by the
Illinois General Assembly and regulations adopted by the Illinois Pollution Control Board which
encourage a tiered approach to remediating environmenta l contamination. T he County enters this
Agreement in the spirit of those laws and pursuant to its rights and obligations as property owner. Should
any part or provision of this Agreement be struck down by a court of competent jurisdiction, this
Agreement shall be null and void.
C.
Notice: All notices required here in shall be in writing and be served personally, by certified or
registered mail, or by facsimile device upon the parties as follows:

D.
Governing Law: This Agreement shall be governed, interpreted and construed according to the
laws of the State of Illinois.
'
E.
Amendment: This Agreement contains the entire agreement of the parties and shall supersede
any prior written or oral agreements or understandings. This Agreement may only be altered, modified or

F.
Compliance with Laws: The parties agree to observe and comply with all federal, state and local
laws which may in any manner affect performance under this Agreement.

OFFICE OF THE CHIEF JUDGE
GRANT AWARD
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 16, 200 I from
HENRY A. BUDZINSKI, Interim Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization to accept a grant in the amount of $250,000.00 from the State of lllinois
Department of Human Services (OHS). This grant will fund an expansion of the court's award winning
continuum of juvenile detention alternatives and dispositional programs. These diversionary programs
are used by judges in the court' s Juvenile Justice Division to address the needs of minors in both the preadjudication and post-dispositional stages of cases. These programs have been directly responsible fo r
reducing overcrowding at the Juvenile Temporary Detention Center over the past five years.
The grant will fund a community-based evening reporting center for girls in the City of Chicago, the first
such alternative detention program for girls in the State of lllinois. The Juveni le Probation and Court
Services Department is in the planning stages for this reporting center and will come before the Board
when a suitable site and service provider have been identified.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $250,000.00. Funding period: July I, 2001 through June
30, 2002.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Interim
Chief Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County be approved and that the Proper Officials be authorized
to sign on behalf of Cook County. The motion carried unanimously.

HENRY A. BUDZINSKI, Interim C hief Judge, C ircuit Court of Cook County

Domestic Relations Court, 28 North Clark Street; and the Sixth Municipal District in south suburban

west suburban Maywood. The Children 's Advocacy C lini c operates in the 1340 South Michigan Avenue
court facil ity .

MEMORANDUM OF AGREEMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 30, 2001 from
HENRY A. BUDZINSK I, Interim C hief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
respectfully requests that the Cook County Board of Commissioners authori ze the County of Cook, on
behalf of the Circ uit Court of Cook County to enter into a proposed Memorandum of Agreement (the
"Agreement") with Loyola Univers ity Medical Center to operate a Children' s Advocacy Center in the
Fourth Municipal District Courthouse in Maywood, Illi nois.
The C ircuit Co urt of Cook County, in conjunction with the County of Cook has developed this
Agreement to memorialize the court's unprecedented partnershi p with Loyola Uni versity Medical Center.
T his partners hip allows for the expansion of the court's cutting edge Children's Advocacy Room program
serving the needs of children and parents caught in the web of domestic violence to west suburban Cook
County. Currentl y seven Children's Advocacy Rooms and one Children' s Advocacy Clinic operate in
court facilities throughout Cook County . T he seven rooms provide safe and nurturing environments
where children may stay while parents or g uardians attend court proceedings. The clinic offers voluntary
mental health assessments for fam il ies involved in domestic violence court.

2585

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
The new Children's Advocacy Center in Maywood will continue the mission of the Children's Advocacy
Rooms program by providing a full spectrum of voluntary social and medical services to children and
families as well as a safe haven in which children may rel ax and play while their parents or guardians
attend court. Working with court personne l, Loyola University Medical Center will staff the clinic with
trained pediatric social work specialists and a child-l ife specialist who will provide health screening
referrals and education for parents and their children. A lso, medical treatment will be available through
the University Medical Center's Ronald McDonald Children's Hospital Mobile Clinic, a fully equipped
pediatric mobile unit staffed with a physician and medical personnel and containing ultrasound and X-ray
equipment, which will stop at the center on a scheduled basis.
Although center operations wi ll require the court to provide staff and furnishings previously provided fo r
in the court's budget, the Agreement will have no fiscal impact on Cook County.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Interim
C hief Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

CONTRACT ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication from
HENRY A. BUDZINSKI, Interim Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to increase by $30,000.00, Contract No. 00-41-155
with Oak Forest Psychological Services, Oak Forest, Illinois, for services for the Adult Probation
Department's Specialized Sex Offender Program.
Oak Forest Psychological Services provides
assessments and treatment services for adult sex offenders sentenced to probation for aggravated criminal
sexual abuse or sexual assault.
Board approved amount 09-19-00:
Increase requested:
Adjusted amount:
Reason:

$ 30,000.00
30,000.00
$ 60,000.00

The Adult Probation Department, Circuit Court of Cook County, initiated the Specialized Sex
Offender Program in 1996. Offenders sentenced to the program are required to attend
specialized counseling for a minimum of two years at a court-approved treatment facility.
Treatment consists of in-depth assessments, weekly group counseling and, if deemed
necessary, individual counseling two times per month. Oak Forest Psychological Services
was previously selected through a formal Request for Proposal (RFP) process in 1999. The
proposed increase is necessary due to the increased number of court-ordered referrals and
covers the remaining term of the contract, expiring on November 30, 200 I .

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $30,000.00. (532-260 Account).

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to increase the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

EMERGENCY PURCHASE
Transmitting a Communication from
CYNTHIA HENDERSON, M.D., M.P.H ., Chief Operating Officer, Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County
requesting approval of payment in the amount of $14,600.00 to Affiliated Steam Equipment Company in
order to replace a stop check valve on the #I boiler at Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County.
This req uest is necessary because the valve has a hole in the casting and cannot be rebuilt. T his is one of
four primary units used to supply the hospital with heat and process steam. T he check valve is ins pected
and certified annually by the Illinois State Fire Marshal and must be replaced in order to pass
certification.
Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County has solicited and obtained three (3) Requests for Proposals for this
work. Affiliated Steam Equipment Company submitted the lowest cost proposal.

OFFICE OF THE PUBLIC DEFENDER
GRANT AWARD
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 23 , 2001 from
J. ROB ERT CASH, Chief Administrative Officer, Office of the Public Defender
requesting authorization to accept a grant award in the amount $77,500.00 from the Bureau of Justice
Assistance of the U.S. Department of Justice for a program entitled Representing Noncitizen Criminal
Defendants in the State of Illinois.
The goal of this program is to enhance the level of legal representation rendered in Illinoi s to indigent
noncitizen defendants facing immi gration consequences as a result of state criminal proceedings. This
goal will be accomplished through the dual objectives of: I) providing public defenders and appoi nted
counsel with a resource (i.e., a reference manual) and training for assessing the potential immigration
consequences of state criminal proceedings, and 2) improving judicial economy by reducing the court
time devoted to post-dispositional motions dealing with unanticipated immigration consequences.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $77 ,500.00. Funding period: June I, 200 I through
November 30, 2002.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Chief
Administrative Officer of the Public Defender' s Office be approved and that the Proper Officials be
authori zed to sign on behalfofCook County. The motion carried unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication, dated August 1, 2001 from
JOHN W. DAVIS, Director, Real Estate Management Division
requesting approval of the submitted lease amendment for the premises in the Cook County
Administration Building with the Grandma Gebhard Company as tenant. The Cook County Board had
previously approved an extension of the three existing leases with this tenant on a month-to-month basis
during ongoing negotiations with the tenant for a stated renewal term. The tenant has now elected not to
renew for a long term, but has agreed to continue to operate a portion of the area until December 3 I,
2001. This will allow the County additional time to market the space, and will minimize any loss of
service to occupants of the building. The base rent and operating pass-through expense for the Dairy
Queen and Muffin Shop will continue at their current levels, as will the rental for the storage space lease.
The County will continue to seek out a new occupant for the food service operation during this period.
Notwithstanding the aforementioned, if a suitable tenant has not been identified, also requested is the
authority to extend this agreement upon its expiration, on a month-to-month basis, at the same terms and
conditions with the present tenant.

GRANT A WARD ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication from
MICHAEL F. SHEAHAN, Sheriff of Cook County
by
ZELDA MARTIN WHITTLER, Undersheriff
Re: Grant #646 - Post Release Reintegration Grant
requesting authori zation to extend the end date from June 29, 2001 through October 3 1, 200 I , for the Post
Release Reintegration Grant. This will allow the Department of Impact Incarceration adequate time to
spend the remaining funds in the grant.
The purpose of this grant is to fund the post release phase of the Cook County Boot Camp program. The
post release phase provides participants with needed support as they transition into their communities
from the Boot Camp site. The phase incl udes ongoing counseling, job search consultation, values
reaffirmation and appropriate supervision.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Funding extension period: June 29, 200 I through October 31 , 2001.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Undersheriff
of Cook County be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

CONTRACTS
Transmitting a Communication from
DENNIS MA NZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State's Attorney's Office
requesting authori zation for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Multi-Systemic Therapy
Services (MST), Charleston, South Carolina, to allow the use of the MST mode l and to train local staff
who implement the MST model. MST Services is an organ ization established in collaboration with
Family Services Research Center and the Medical University of South Carolina that provides licensed
traini ng and ongoing research of the MST treatment model. Multi-Systemic Therapy Services is a fami ly
and community based treatment system devised to address and treat the factors withi n a juvenile's family,
peer and school networks which encourage the individual to commit offensive acts. MST Services rel ies
on decades of research to address the known determinants of serious antisocial behavior in youths.
Compared to usual juvenile justice service, MST Services results in significant reduced rates of
incarceration and re-arrest among violent and chronic juvenile offenders.
Reason:

This contract is central to Project Reclaim which is funded by a Juvenile Accountability
Incentive Block Grant (JAIBG). The entire program is based on the multi-systemic therapy
model for treatment of juvenile offenders, for which MST Services is the only trainer in the
country. MST Services has an exclusive license agreement with the Medical University of
South Carolina to train service agencies in the multi-systemic therapy model deve loped by the
researchers at the Medical Uni versity of South Carolina and Dr. Scott W. Henggeler, Family
Research Center, Department of Psychi atry and Behavioral Sciences, Medical University of
South Carolina.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant fu nded amount: $86,992.00. Contract period: April I , 2001
through September 30, 200 I. (833-260 Account). Requisition No. 18330212.

2614

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication from
DENNIS MANZKE, Chiefofthe Administrative Services Bureau, State's Attorney's Office
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Community Mental Health
Council, Inc., Chicago, Illinois, for services and interventions to juveniles as designed by Multi-Systemic
Therapy (MST) Services. Community Mental Health Council, Inc. will be the local provider of the MST
model. The Council will provide adult and child/adolescent outpatient services, case management, crisis
intervention, psychiatric services, residential treatment, research community education and support,
vocational and student training, psycho-social rehabilitation, and mentally ill/substance abuse services.
The Community Mental Health Council, Inc. also provides direct therapeutic services to victims,
witnesses, and significant others of sexual assault, murder, domestic violence, and other violent crimes.
Reason:

Community Mental Health Council, Inc. will be available 24 hours a day to participate in and
provide community based, family focused services to referred juveniles and their families.
The Community Mental Health Council, Inc. has an extensive 25-year history of service to
the Chicago and suburban areas of Cook County. They were chosen because of their
extensive experience in the mental health field and its emphasis on violence issues as it
relates to youths.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funded amount: $200,000.00. Contract period: April I, 2001
through September 30, 2001. (833-260 Account). Requisition No. 18330213.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

positive working relationship with the Cook County Juvenile Court providing an array of
diversion as well as pre-adjudication and post-adjudication services. The agency administers
local, state and federal funds which promote positive outcomes for youth, fam ilies and
communities.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001

OFFICE OF THE COUNTY TREASURER
PROPOSED CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
MICHAEL J. SHINE, Chief Deputy Treasurer
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Aston Group, Chicago,
Illinois, to provide Microsoft Great Plains e-Enterprise General Ledger Accounting Software.
The office prepared and distributed a Request for Proposal (RFP) for General Ledger Accounting
Software in May 200 I . Six potential vendors received a copy of the RFP. The following fo ur ( 4)
responses were received:
1. Epicor Software Corporation
2. Aston Group (Navision)
3. Aston Group (Microsoft Great Plains)
4. Mitchell Humphrey
The office evaluated the responses based on various criteria. The criteria included, but was not limited to:
•
•
•
•
•
•
•

Can the system accommodate additional detailed account information?
Does the system provide an audit trail for all transactions?
Is your company certified as a Minority-owned Business Enterprise (MBE) or Woman-owned
Business Enterprise (WBE)?
Does the system provide security for posting, viewing, and reporting?
Provide the ability to drill down to transaction source?
Environmentally and strategically compatible with the Treasurer's Office current technical
environment?
Ability to interface with other financial systems?

Based on the results of the office's evaluation, Aston Group (Microsoft Great Plains) ranked higher than
the other firms responding.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $323,000.00. Contract period: September I, 2001 through August I, 2002.
(7 I 7/060-579 Account). Requisition No. 10600084.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved that the communication be referred
to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 245573). The motion carried unanimously.

DONALD E. PELOQUIN, Mayor of the City of Blue Island
Re:

NO CASH BID PROPOSAL

On behalf of the residents of the City of Blue Island, we are requesting your assistance in securing a tax
delinquent property on a no cash bid basis from the County scavenger sale. This property has been an
eyesore for the residents that have lived next to it for years. The city's building department has tried
numerous times to contact the property owner to no avail. We are trying to secure an abandon industrial
building to be developed according to the proposal made by C & H Partners to the City Council. The
City of Blue Island will be responsible for all legal expenses.

29-06- 104-001-0000

29-06-103-004-0000
29-06-103-003-0000

Committee on Finance Tax Delinquency Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 245577). The motion carried
unanimously.

This firm represents the Village of Matteson relative to this Application. T he purpose of this letter is to
advise you of the Village's desire to continue its pa rticipation in the Cook County No Cash Bid Program.
The Village is interested in acquiring the following parcels in its community that have deli nquent real
estate taxes for two or more years, pursuant to 35 ILCS 200/2 1-90. Please accept this request to obtain
said properties which are also listed on the submitted Exhibi t "A". Said parcels are located in Matteson,
Illinois.
PIN 3 1- 16-302-007 (Parcel I) is located adjacent to property currently owned by the Village. PIN 3 1-16302-009 (Parcel 2) is located directly across the street from Parcel I. The parcels are located within a
natural storm water storage area as determi ned by the Village's official flood plain map. Some of the
property contai ns wetlands. The purpose for acq uiri ng these properties is to mai ntain them in their
natural state as storm water retention and to serve as passive recreation areas for neighboring
subdi visions. The Village will develop nature trails and observation points for appreciation of the native
prairie, wetland plants, and numerous bird species. There are no third party applicants.

236033

A RESOLUTION SEEKING REMEDY TO THE HARDSHIPS EXPERIENCED BY THE
CITIZENS OF COOK COUNTY CAUSED BY THE PRACTICE OF PREDATORY
LENDING BY CERTAIN SUB-PRIME LENDING INSTITUTIONS (PROPOSED
RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Earlean Collins and Jerry
Butler, County Commissioners:
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

SEEKING REMEDY TO THE HARDSHIPS EXPERIENCED BY THE CITIZENS
OF COOK COUNTY CAUSED BY THE PRACTICE OF PREDATORY LENDING
BY CERTAIN SUB-PRIME LENDING INSTITUTIONS
WHEREAS, foreclosures are a growing problem in Cook County, they have grown by
92 .5% from 1993 to 1998, a five (5) year period; and

2651

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDI NGS FOR AUGUST 9, 200 1

WHEREAS, sub-prime lenders were involved in thirty (30) foreclosures in 1993, they were
involved in one thousand four hundred seventeen ( 1417) in 1998; and
WHEREAS, the lending practice of many sub-prime lenders has been found to be predatory
and a major contributor to the increase in the rate of foreclosures within Cook County.
Predatory lending occurs when a mortgage banker or broker engages directly or indirectly in
the practice of home equity loans through the use of high pressure marketing tactics,
excessive interest rates, and loan repayment plans that are beyond the homeowner' s fi nancial
ability to repay; and
WHEREAS, this problem is widespread throughout Cook County affecting all communities
and c itizens at all economic levels.
THEREFORE THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS calls upon the
Treasurer of Cook County to require all bidding banks and savi ngs and loan associations
seeking to be a depository of Cook County funds provide to the Treasurer an affidavit
certifying that it nor any of its affiliates are involved in the practice of predatory lending.

* Referred to the Committee on Finance May 16, 2000.

CLERK OF THE CIRCU IT COURT, Dorothy Brown, transmitti ng a Communication :
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with the
NATIONAL CENTER FOR STATE COURTS (NCSC), Denver, Colorado, to develop an
Information Technology strategic plan for the Clerk of the Circuit Court. The NCSC will
review the business processes and the current technology in the Clerk's Office. The NCSC,
in conjunction with a steering committee, will define the appropriate changes in business
process and the technology needs of the Clerk's Office and provide recommendations for
business change and alternative technology solutions.

2652

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
Reason:

than 29 years of experience in assisting courts in determining and devising
solutions to court issues. In addition, the NCSC has deve loped a cadre of
specialists in the various aspects of court operations and wi II draw upon many of
these individuals in this project.

244839

VITAL RECORDS FEES FOR THE COUNTY CLERK (PROPOSED ORDINANCE).
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance from David Orr, County C lerk.
PROPOSED ORDI NANCE

VITAL RECORDS FEES FOR THE COUNTY CLERK
WHEREAS, the Cook County Clerk maintains marriage, birth, and death records for Cook
County; and
WHEREAS, the 92nd Illinois General Assembly passed H.B. 3054, a bi ll that amends the
Yita i Records Act; and
WHEREAS, H.B . 3054 requires county clerks and local registrars to charge a $2 .00 fee for
each certified copy of a death registration, in addition to any other fees charged by county
clerks and local registrars; and
WHEREAS, H.B. 3054 provides that the $2 .00 fee must be transmitted to the State Registrar
monthly and deposited into the Death Certificate Surcharge Fund for the purpose of
implementing a statewide e lectronic report ing system for death registrations and for other
purposes; and
WHEREAS, it is expected that the Governor wi ll sign H.B . 3054 into law, which wo uld take
immediate effect; and
WHEREAS, the City of Chicago currently charges $I 0.00 for first copies of death
certificates and $2.00 for additional copies; and

2655

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001

WHEREAS, the Cook County Clerk currently charges $7.00 for first copies of death
certificates and $2.00 for additional copies.

NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1. The Cook County Clerk shall continue to charge and collect a fee of$7.00 for the
first copy, and $2.00 for each additional copy of a birth record.

Section 2. The Cook County Clerk shall continue to charge and collect a fee of $7 .00 for the
first copy, and $2.00 for each additional copy of a marriage record.

Section 3. The Cook County Clerk shall charge and collect a fee of $ 10.00 for the first
copy, and $4.00 for each additional copy of a death record.

Section 4. The fee increase for death records s hall become effective upon passage of this
Ordinance, but not until such time as H.B. 3054 becomes law.

* Referred to the Committee on Finance July 10, 2001.
Commissioner Moran inquired if the State of Illinois or the Veterans' Assistance Commission have a
provision for free vital records for veterans?
Brandon Neese, Deputy County C lerk, answered that he will confirm the information and respond to the
Committee.

Vice Chairman Carr, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Ordinance (Comm. No.
244839) be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
01-0-19
ORDINANCE

VITAL RECORDS FEES FOR THE COUNTY CLERK
WHEREAS, the Cook County Clerk maintains marriage, birth, and death records for Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the 92nd Jllinois General Assembly passed H.B. 3054, a bill that amends the Yitai Records
Act; and

WHEREAS, H.B. 3054 requires county clerks and local registrars to charge a $2.00 fee for each certified
copy of a death registration, in addition to any other fees charged by county clerks and local registrars;
and
WHEREAS, H.B. 3054 provides that the $2.00 fee must be transmitted to the State Registrar monthly
and deposited into the Death Certificate Surcharge Fund for the purpose of implementing a statewide
electronic reporting system for death registrations and for other purposes; and
WHEREAS, it is expected that the Governor will sign H.B. 3054 into Jaw, which would take immediate
effect; and

2656

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS, the City of Chicago currently charges $I 0.00 for first copies of death certificates and $2.00
for additional copies; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Clerk currently charges $7.00 for first copies of death certificates and
$2.00 for additional copies.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1. The Cook County C lerk shall continue to charge and collect a fee of$7.00 for the first copy,
and $2.00 for each additional copy of a birth record.
Section 2. T he Cook County C lerk shall continue to charge and collect a fee of $7 .00 for the first copy,
and $2.00 for each additional copy of a marriage record.
Section 3. The Cook County Clerk shall charge and col lect a fee of $10.00 for the first copy, and $4.00
for each additional copy of a death record.
Section 4. The fee increase for death records shall become effective upon passage of this Ordinance, but
not until such time as H.B. 3054 becomes law.

244841

LEGAL DESCRIPTION AUTOMATION FEE FOR THE COUNTY CLERK (PROPOSED
ORDINANCE). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance from David Orr, County Clerk.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
LEGAL DESCRIPTION AUTOMATION FEE FOR THE COUNTY CLERK
WHEREAS, the Cook County Clerk maintai ns records of official legal descriptions on over
2 million c urrent and former permanent real index numbers in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the only format in which these records currentl y exist is a manual copy of the
records created since the institution of the permanent real estate index system over forty-five
years ago; and
WHEREAS, the County Clerk would like to both preserve and automate these legal
description records so legal descriptions can be accessible in conjunction with the countywide
GlS;and
WHEREAS, the County Clerk's Office is currently working to implement the GlS project
through review and analysis of digitized versions of the Clerk's official county tax maps and
ancillary property records; and

2657

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001

WHEREAS, the Industrial Engineering Section of the Bureau of Administration has
determined that the cost to produce a legal description upon request justifies an increase in
the fee to help defray costs to automate and preserve these records; and
WHEREAS, the Industrial Engineers have further determined that is very important that all
complete legal descriptions be accessible through the county's new GIS system and that there
is no other source avai lable for this information:
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1. That the County Clerk shall charge and collect a fee of $3.00 from each party
who purchases a copy of a legal description in the County of Cook to be
deposited in the (County) Clerk's Automation Fund;

Section 2. This fee shall be in addition to all other fees and charges of the Clerk and shall be
remitted monthly by the C lerk to the County Treasurer in the special fund
designated as the Clerk's Automation Fund;

Section 3. The County Clerk shall commence such charges and collections beginning two
weeks after passage;

Section 4. This Ordinance shall become effective upon passage.

* Referred to the Committee on Finance July 10, 2001.
Commissioner Maldonado asked Fredda Berman, Director of Real Estate & Tax Services for the County
Clerk' s Office, what is the estimated cost for the automation process?
Ms. Berman stated she currently does not know the cost.
Mrs. O'Leary responded the expected cost of the project would be $150,000.
For the record, Chairman Daley stated he submitted questions to the Clerk's Office regarding the
proposed ordinance. (The referenced document is on file in the Office of the County Clerk.)

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the Ordinance (Comm. No.
244841) be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

245236

REGINALD JOHNSON , Laborer for the Highway Department
Dateoflnjury: May 10, 1999
Case Number: 99-WC-61227
Amount of Recovery: None
On May 10, I 999, Reginald Johnson allegedly sustained accidental injuries arising out of and
in the course of his employment as a Laborer for the Highway Department. The accident
occurred when the Petitioner was sitting in a Highway Department vehicle when another
vehicle drove into the back of the truck. The Petitioner suffered injuries to his head, neck,
back and right ankle.
The County paid a total of $4,002.86 in temporary total disability benefits and $781.19 in
medical expenses for a total of $4, 784.05. The County is entitled to recover 75% of that
amount, which is $3 ,588.04. The County has agreed with the Petitioner and his counsel to
waive the lien in full in exchange for his waiver of the right to payment for permanent partial
disability and future medical expenses.
The Finance Subcommittee on Industrial Claims approved to the waiving of the lien on June
I 2, 200 I. Therefore, we request Board approval of the lien waiver.

Lien Waiver:

None
$3,588.04

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
245253

EARNESTINE HOSKINS, Juvenile Court Clerk
Date oflnjury: December 14, 1995
Case Number: 96-WC-00524
Amount of Recovery: $8,333.00
On December 14, 1995, Earnestine Hoskins, a Clerk with the Juvenile Court Clerk's Office
slipped and fell in a parking lot injuring her hand, knees and back. The Petitioner suffered a
herniated disc at C3-4 with impingement of the thecal sac.
Ms. Hoskins filed a third party lawsuit against General Parking Corporation for $25,000 .00.
The County has a lien to recover its Workers' Compensation expenditures.
Cook County paid Workers' Compensation benefits of $15,540.00 for permanent partial
disabi lity. Pursuant to the Illinois Workers' Compensation Act, the County is entitled to
recover 75% of its lien, which totals $11,655.00.
The Defendants offered to settle the third party case for $25,000.00. The County has agreed
to accept $8,333 .00 of the settlement proceeds. This means the County would reduce its lien
by $3,322.00.
The Finance Subcommittee on Industrial Claims approved the reduction of the County's lien
on May 8, 2001. Therefore, we request Board approval of the lien reduction reflecting a net
recovery of$8,333.00.
$8,333.00
$3,322.00

Lien Waiver:

ORDINANCE
Transmi tting a Communication, dated August 7, 200 I from
KAREN L. SCOTT, M.D., M.P.H., Chief Operating Officer, Department of Public Health
requesting ap proval of the following amendment to Cook County Ordinance 5-2 I 4, which authorizes the
Cook County Department of Public Health to charge for the search and certification of birth and death
records in its capacity as the Vital Records Registrar for Illinois Registrar District I 6.0, to increase the
fees charged.
A recently enacted State law requires the collection of a new $2.00 fee for each first and fo r each
additional certified copy of death or fetal death record. These fees are to be transmitted to the Illinois
Department of Public Health's Death Certification Surcharge Fund. In addition to the required $2.00 fee
increase, the Cook County Department of Public Health is also requesting another $1.00 fee increase on
the first copy of each death record to ma ke its charges consistent with those c harged by the Cook County
C lerk.
Esti mated fi scal impact: Net revenue increase estimate of $15,000.00 for a 12 month period.

OJ-0-21
ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING C OOK COUNTY ORDINANCE 5-214,
DEPARTMENT OF P UBLIC HEALTH SEARCH AND
CER TIFICATION FEES, AS AMENDED
WHEREAS, The County of Cook is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to the 1970
Illinois Constitution; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to its home rule powers the Board of Cook County Commissioners
adopted Cook County Ordinance 5-2 14 setting the fees fo r the Department of Public Health in the search
and certification of birth, death a nd fetal death records; and

2775

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS, pursuant to 410 ILCS 535/25 ( I), the Department of Public Health may charge fees
which may not exceed the fees charged by the State Registrar of $ 10.00 for the search and certification of
s uch records, an additional fee of $5.00 for a certified copy of such records and $2.00 for each additional
certification or certified copy requested; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Clerk and the City of Chicago currently charge $10.00 for the
initial search and certification of a death certificate; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to P.A. 92-0 141 , and effective July 24, 200 I, which amends 410 ILCS
535/25, the Department of Public Health as a local registrar, must charge a $2.00 surcharge fee for each
certified copy of a death certificate. The fee is in addition to any other fees that are charged by the local
registrar. The additional fees must be transmitted to the Illinois Department of Public Health monthly for
deposit into the Death Certificate Surcharge Fund for purposes of establi shing an electronic reporting
system; and
WHEREAS, the amendment to 410 ILCS 535/25 now restricts the local registrar from assessing
fees against an organization chartered by Congress that requires a certificate for the purpose of death
verification.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF THE
COUNTY OF COOK, ILLINOIS, AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1.
5-214

Cook County Ordinance 5-214, as amended, is hereby amended as follows;
SEARCH ANDCERTIFlCATIONS FEES

a) The Department of Public Health shall charge a fee of $7.00 for any search of the files of
birth records and $ 10.00 for any search of the files of death and fetal death records upon a written request
from an applicant entitled to such search. If, upon search, the record request is found, the custodian to
whom the request was submitted shall furni sh the applicant one certification of such record, or one
certified copy of such record.
b) A further fee of $2.00 shall be required for each additional certification or certified copy
requested of a birth record and $4.00 for each additional certification or certified copy requested of a
death or fetal death record.
c) The Department of Public Health is hereby authorized to initiate transmittal of fees to the
State Registrar collected for the Death Certification Surcharge Fund as requ ired by law.
d) The Department of Public Health shall waive the fee for any death certification requested by
an organization chartered by Congress for the purpose of death verification.
Section 2. This amendment shall be effective upon passage.

Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to suspend the rules so that
this matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Ordinance be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

2776

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 200 I
RESOLUTIONS
01-R-534
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE WILLIAM R. MORAN COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
ALLAN C. CARR EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ, ROBERTO MALDONADO
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND CALVIN R. SUTKER COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, VA Lakeside Medical Center was integrated with the Veterans Affairs Chicago Health Care
System in 1996; and
WHEREAS, Lakeside, located in downtown Chicago, offers primary, secondary and tertiary care to the
areas 400,000 veterans; and
WHEREAS, Lakeside has 128 authorized beds and has treated 4,500 inpatients and 120,000 outpatients
in Fiscal Year 2000; and
WHEREAS, for most veterans, entry into the VA healthcare system is the only health service they have;
and
WHEREAS, veteran service organizations and other individual and group volunteers are active and have
donated over 36,600 hours of service in Fiscal Year 2000; and
WHEREAS, if VA Lakeside Medical Center were to close its doors, the abi lity to access benefits by
veterans would provide an atmos phere that is not conducive to VA policy; and
WHEREAS, this is another obstacle the veterans of Cook County must overcome; and
WHEREAS, the VA healthcare system has enhanced its image by commitment, sacrifice, and spirit to
serve veterans at the VA Lakeside Medical Center; and
WHEREAS, Lakeside must continue to carry the torch towards keeping its doors open to address the
needs of those who have served our country.
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and the Cook County Board of
Commiss ioners encourages President George W. Bush, Congress, and the Veterans Administration to
continue to serve Cook County veterans at VA Lakeside Medical Center; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that special attention should be provided to the Cook County veterans'
population, and ensure healthcare for our veterans.

2777

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
