Transmitting a Communication, dated July 13, 2001 from
GWENDOLYN D. CLEMONS, Director, Department of Planning and Development
Re: Financial Applications Corp.
Resolution Approving Class 6b Special Exception to Abandonment
Respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding the Company's application for Class 6b property tax
incentive for your consideration.
Financial Applications Corp. request approval of the special exception to the 24 month vacancy rule
under the Class 6b Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the Company can complete its
application to the Assessor of Cook County.
Submitting the Financial Application Corp. application for Class 6b, the Resolution of the Village of
Tinley Park, and a Department of Planning and Development staff report for your information.

01-R-537
RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 6b which provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for an industrial facility;
and

2782

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires the approval by the County Board of a special exception for abandonment
in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive months upon
purchase; and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an app lication from
Financial Applications Corp. and the Resolution of the Village of Tinley Park for a vacant industrial
facility located at 7420 Duvan Drive in Tinley Park, Bremen Township, Cook County, Property Index
Numbers 27-36-205-026 and 27-36-205-033 ; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the granting of a 6b Real
Estate Classification to Financial Applications Corp. will be beneficial to the County; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commi ssioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for 16 months at the time of application in July, 200 1, and that special circumstances are present and that
th is incentive is necessary for the productive reuse of the building to occur.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and the Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and the Board of Commissioners support and consent
to the application of Financial Applications Corp. for a facility located at 7420 Duvan Drive, Tinley Park,
Bremen Township, Cook County under the provision of C lass 6b abatement incentive for abandonment of
less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.
A pp roved and adopted this 9th day of August 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Burnham Car Wash, Inc. requests approval of the special exception to the 24 month vacancy rule under
the Class 7a Ordinance. Thi s Resolution is required so that the Company can complete its application to

Ol-R-538
RESOLUTION
WHEREA S, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 7a which provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for a commercial
facility; and
WHEREAS, Class 7a requires the approval by the County Board of a special exception for abandonment
in cases where the commercial facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive months upon
purchase; and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application fro m
Burnham Car Wash, Inc., Illinois, for a vacant portion of commercial faci lity located at 18600 South
Burnham, Lansing, Illinois, Cook County, Illinois, Property Index Numbers 33-06-20 1-029; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the granting of a 7a Real
Estate Classification to Burnham Car Wash, Inc. will be beneficial to the County; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the build ing was abandoned
for seventeen months at the date of purchase and that this incentive is necessary for use of the building to
occur and that the Cook County Board of Commissioners supports and consents to the Class 7a
Application fo r the special exception for abandoned property for Jess than 24 months of vacancy to be
submitted to the Cook County Assessor.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and the Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and the Board of Commissioners indicate their
approval to the granting of a Cook County Real Estate Classification 7a abatement incentive to Burnham
Car Wash, Inc. fo r a vacant portion of a commercial faci lity located at 18600 South Burnham, Lansing,
Illinois, Cook County, Illinois; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authori zed and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.

01-R-539
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN P. DALEY, PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.,
CALVIN R. SUTKER AND TED LECHOWICZ
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst,

The Honorable Daniel J. White
born into time June 24, 1922
passed into eternity July 15, 2001 , and
WHEREAS Daniel J. White was the beloved husband of Sandie Doherty-White and the late Laverne
White, nee Goetzinger, and
WHEREAS Daniel J. White was the devoted father of Daniel (Nanette), Patricia (Timothy) Coleman ,
Therese (Thomas) Flemp and Brian (fiancee Maureen) White, and was the loving grandfather of 18 and
great-grandfather of one, and
WHEREAS Dani el J. White graduated from Lindblom High School, attended St. Benedict's College in
Kansas, Loyola University in Chicago and graduated from the John Marshall School of Law in 1951 , and
WHEREAS Daniel J. White answered the call of his country during World War 11, where he served the
cause of freedom in the United States Army with uncommon valor and distinction, and he later served
stateside as an American Legion post commander, and
WHEREAS Dan iel J. White served as an assistant Illinois attorney general from 1951- 1953 , in the City
of Chicago corporation counsel's office from 1953- 1960, 1964, and was named a Circuit Court magistrate
in 1964, and
WHEREAS Daniel J. White was appointed to the bench in 1971 and served in the criminal division
until 198 1, and as chief judge of Traffic Court from 198 1-1 987, when he resigned to serve in the law
division until his retirement in 1996, and
WHEREAS Daniel J. White was a three-term member of the Illinois State Bar Association Board of
Governors, a board member at Holy Cross Hospital, Chicago Boys Clubs of America and Haymarket
House, and

2785

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS all who knew him will attest that Judge White was a jurist of the highest order, known for
his professional demeanor, virtue beyond reproach, fair-minded and reasoned decisions, and his mastery
of the practice of Jaw, now therefore
BE IT RESOLVED by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that the Board does hereby offer its
deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and many friends of Daniel J. White, and
joins them in sorrow at this time of loss, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body, and a suitable copy of same be tendered to the family of Daniel J. White, that his memory may be
so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Honoring the 50th Anniversary of Villa Scalabrini
WHEREAS, the year 2001 marks the 50th Anniversary of Villa Scalabrini ; and
WHEREAS, the July 29, 2001 anniversary party celebrates the life and accomplishments of the fo under
of the Villa, the Reverend Armando Pierini ; and
WHEREAS, in the early 1940s, Father Pierini issued a call to the Chicago-area Italian-American
community to donate their time, resources and energy toward the creation of a nursing home for the
elderly; and

2786

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS, since July 1951 when the Villa was dedicated, it has grown into one of the finest nursing
homes in the state, thanks in large part to the charismatic leadership of Father Pierini and the remarkable
generosity of the Italian-American community and the community at large; and
WHEREAS, the Missionary Sisters of St. Charles who live and work at the Villa have played a
significant role in making the Villa the wonderful place it is today; and
WHEREAS , the Villa is now owned by the Sisters of the Holy Family and the Sisters of the Res urrection
who continue to foster its special place in the heart of the community.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Board of Commissioners of Cook
County does hereby congratulate Villa Scalabrini on its 50th Anniversary and acknowledge its many
contributions to the residents of the County of Cook; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered for presentation to
Villa Scalabrini as evidence of the esteem in which it is held by this Honorable Body and by the residents
of Cook County.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 200 1.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County C lerk
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. T he motion carried unanimously.

01-R-541
RESOLUTION

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TED LECHOWICZ, PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
AND JOHN P. DALEY, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by

HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WH EREAS, the County Board has learned wi th sorrow of the death of the Honorable Walter J.
Kowalski, Judge of the C ircuit Court of Cook County; and
WH EREAS, Walter J. Kowalski's service as a judge extended over 47 years; and

2787

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS, Judge Kowalski was appointed to the Cook County Probate Court in 1954; and
WHEREAS, in 1956 Judge Kowalski was elected to the [former] Chicago Municipal Court; and
WHEREAS, Judge Kowalski was elected a Circuit Judge in 1966 and served for 35 years in that
capacity (being recalled to the bench by the Illinois Supreme Court every year since 1996); and
WHEREAS, Judge Kowalski was known for hi s work ethic and for his ability to facilitate
settlement of difficult and complex cases; and
WHEREAS, Judge Kowalski was honored as "Trial Judge of the Year" of the American Board of
Trial Advocates in 1999; and
WHEREAS, Walter J. Kowalski also served his country as a member of the U.S. Army during
World War 11 , and as an employee of the Manhattan Project and the Atomic Energy Commission after the
war; and
WHEREAS, Judge Kowalski served the people of this State and County with distinction during
his long tenure in public office; and
WHEREAS, Walter J. Kowalski leaves to cherish his memory his wife, Sue; his son, the
Honorable Robert J. Kowalski, Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County; his daughters, Arlene
Kowal ski and Ricky Schwed; his grandchildren, Lauren, Melissa, Deanna, Jonathan, Kristin, Mark, Allen
and Sharon; five great-grandchildren, and many other fami ly members and friends; and
WHEREAS, Walter J. Kowalski will be missed by all who knew him.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
does hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Judge Walter J. Kowalski, offers its heartfelt
sympathy to hi s fami ly in their hour of sorrow and loneliness, for their loss is shared by al l Members of
this Honorable Body and the people of the County of Cook, and join his fami ly and friends in honoring
his memory; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the fam ily
of Judge Walter J. Kowalski as a memorial of his good works and also spread upon the official
proceeding of thi s Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 200 I.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst,
DAVIDE. FRIEDLER
WHEREAS, David E. Friedler was the beloved husband for 50 years of Maya, loving father of Eric and
Mindy, devoted grandfather of Jennie, Annie, Emmy and Molly, dear brother of William and Sylvia, and
brother-in-law of Seymour and Adele, Gerald and Geraldine, and
WHEREAS, David E. Friedler grew up on C hicago's West Side and graduated from Marshall High
School. He met hi s wife when he was just 7 years of age. Their eventual marriage was "a great love
affair" and they raised their children in Evanston before moving back to C hicago, and
WHEREAS, David E. Friedler bravely served his country as a Navy diver in the Pacific during World
War II, and
WHEREAS, David E. Friedler returned from the war and worked as a mortgage broker and later
became a self-made fixture on the city' s real estate scene, and
WHEREAS, David E. Friedler was an ardent supporter of the peace and femin ist movements of the
1960s and '70s, and upheld the cause by helping stranded Grant Park protesters during the 1968
Democratic National Conventio n, and
WHEREAS, David E. Friedler formed his own construction company in 1988, Friedler Construction
Company of Chicago, and
WHEREAS, David E. Friedler was honored w hen he received the "Richard H. Driehaus Award" for the
Humboldt Park Stables renovation, and
WHEREAS, David E. Friedler was devoted to his family, his fai th and his community and left a legacy
of dedication to his profession a nd fam ily and great love of life.

2789

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 200 1
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of David E. Friedler, and offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
family in their hour of sorrow and joins his family in honoring his memory, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the fami ly of

01-R-544
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONER

AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, on April 18, 1936, Monsignor Ignatius D. McDermott was duly ordained a Catholic
priest, and
WHEREAS, Monsignor D. McDermott has recently celebrated the 65th Anniversary of his ordination
and his 65th year of service to the Catholic Archdiocese of Chicago, and
WHEREAS, Monsignor McDermott, a native Chicagoan, studied at Quigley Preparatory Seminary and
Mundelein's St. Mary of the Lake Seminary. He received a Masters of Social Work from Loyola
University in 1970 and a Certificate from the Yale School of Alcohol Studies in 1957. The commute to a
summer job in 1930 at Arlington Park Racetrack introduced Monsig nor McDermott to the Skid Row
neighborhood and the plight of its victims. This experience would lead to a lifetime commitment to better
the lives of those affected by the disease of alcoholism, and the appellation bestowed upon him, "Apostle
of the Alcoholics", and
WHEREAS, Monsignor McDermott was assigned to the staff at Maryville Academy, a home for
dependant children in Des Plaines, from 1936 -1941. He served as assistant pastor of Our Lady of Peace
from 194 J -1946 in the then affluent South Shore neighborhood. It was here that Father Mac came to
believe that alcoholism was a disease and not a social problem of the less fortunate of society, and that it
had a tendency to be inherited, and
WHEREAS, Monsignor McDermott was named in 1946 as assistant director of the Chicago
Archdiocese's Catholic Charities and executive director of the Catholic Dependent Child Commission.
He s imultaneously served as director of Holy Cross Mission, an agency administering to the corporal and
spiritual needs of Skid Row inhabitants. Father McDennott developed an alcohol education curriculum
for the Chicago school system and fostered Alternatives to Expulsion, a program incorporated into State
of Illinois educational practices, and
WHEREAS, Monsignor McDermott founded in 1963 the internationally recog nized Central States
Institute of Addiction (CSIA), which offers in-depth training for individuals, group associations, and
professionals involved in handling addictions. At this time he also founded the state's first "Driving
Under the Influence Program" called Alcohol and Drug Assessment Services (ADAS) which became the
model for the programs now used throughout the nation. In 1979 he founded Intervention Instruction as a
substance abuse education-prevention agency, and

2792

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001

WHEREAS, Monsignor McDermott founded Haymarket House in 1975 as president of the Chicago
C lergy Association for the Homeless Person. It was the first freestanding, social setting detoxification
center in Ill inois. Haymarket House has since expand ed to a large complex known as the McDermott
Center providing a detoxification center, food and shelter for the homeless, counseli ng, drug abuse
services, famil y support and a Maternal Addiction Unit. Under Father McDermott's guidance, the Center
offers dig nity and self-respect to the approximately 1,000 people admitted to the facili ty each week, and
WHEREAS, Monsignor McDermott has been honored w ith numerous awards fo r his trail-blazing
solutions to the homeless and substance abuse problems recurrent in our society. He most recently
received the "200 I John H. McDermott Award for Civic Leadership'', the "2000 Human itari an for the
Millennium Award" and the" 1999 Light in the Darkness Award", and
WHEREAS, Monsignor McDermott possesses an indefatigable spirit exemplified by countl ess acts of
generosity, integrity, humility and unswerving dedication to his faith and improving the lives of others.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby congratulate Monsignor Ignatius McDermott on the occasion of the 65th Anniversary of his
ordinat ion to the Catho lic priesthood and wish him many more years of good health and happiness, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Monsignor
Ignatius McDermott as recognition of his immeasu rable achievements and benevolent works and also
spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable Body.
A pp roved and adopted this 9th day of August 200 I .
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA Y ID ORR, Co unty C lerk

2796

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 200 1

WHEREAS, Geza von Molnar was born in Leipzig, Germany in 1932 and survived the Holocaust with
the help of a governess who protected him after his mother escaped to New York, and a farmer's wife
who hid him in Hungary. He moved to New York in 1947, became a U.S. citizen and served in the U.S.
Air Force from 1950- 1954, and

WHEREAS, Geza von Molnar was an exceptional scholar and graduated magna cum laude from Hunter
Col lege in New York with a bachelor's degree in German and Philosophy in 1958. He earned his
master's degree in German in 1960 and a doctorate in German and the Humanities Honors Program in
1966 from Stanford University, and
WHEREAS, Geza von Molnar's long and distinguished teaching career began at Northwestern
University in 1963. He was named a professor in 1983 and chaired the German Department three times
for a total of ten years. Mr. von Molnar served as director of the university's program in European
Thought and Culture from 1989. "We have lost an extraordinary leader, teacher and scholar," said Eric
Sundquist, dean of the Weinberg College of Arts and Sciences at Northwestern. " Geza's devotion to his
students and colleagues was matched by his dedicated service, in many ways over many years, to
Northwestern'', and

WHEREAS, Geza von Molnar was respected by his students and colleagues alike. He would enliven
his lectures with anecdotes of his compelling life story. " He was a really warm and caring father figure
and mentor," said Franziska Lys, assistant chair of the German department. " He wanted his students to
succeed. His door was always open", and

WHEREAS, Geza von Molnar was the author of numerous scholarly articles and chapters and
frequently spoke at national and international conferences. He also wrote two books on the lyric poet
Novalis, Nova/is Fichte Studies: The foundations ofhis Aesthetics and Romantic Vision, Ethical Context:
Nova/is and Artistic Autonomy, and another on Johann Wolfgang von Goethe. Mr. von Molnar's
academic honors included fellowships from the National Endowment for the Humanities and the
American Council of Learned Societies, and
WHEREAS, Geza von Molnar was exceedingly generous with hi s time and served on many of
Northwestern's major committees dealing with financial matters, promotions, curriculum, study abroad,
language study, research s upport and program development, and

WHEREAS, Geza von Molnar was an ardent environmentalist for over two decades. It was his great
love of Winnetka and the surrounding area that led him to take a leadership role in the long, successful
tight to save the Greenbay Trail. Walking and marveling at the nature throughout his community was as
much a part of hi s life as academia had become, and

WHEREAS, Geza von Molnar was passionate ly dedicated to his profession and his community and left
an enduring legacy of devotion to his family, educating and enriching the lives of others, the pursuit of
knowledge and a great love of nature.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Geza von Molnar, and offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
fami ly in their hour of sorrow and joins hi s fami ly in honoring his memory, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a s uitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the fami ly of
Geza von Molnar as a memorial of his good works and spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.

WHEREAS, Tad J. Kimura was born in San Pedro, California. He left high school to manage the
family farm after his father died. Mr. Kimura volunteered for the Army during World War II but was sent
to the interment camp in Poston, Arizona, and
WHEREAS, Tad J. Kimura served his country when he was recruited for Army intelligence during
World War II. He was stationed in Minnesota and taught Japanese to soldi ers there and helped crack
Japanese codes, and
WHEREAS, Tad J. Kimura moved to Chicago before the end of the war and attended DeVry Institute
of Technology to learn television repair. He settled in Morton Grove in 1946 and opened his own
business, Tad's TV and Radio Service, which he ran fo r 45 years. Mr. Kimura was a life member of the
local historical society, joined the American Legion and helped resurrect the Chamber of Commerce, and
WHEREAS, Tad J. Kimura was ardently dedicated to hi s community and volunteered fo r the village's
volunteer fire department in 1952. He served as captain of the rescue squad and established CPR and first
aid training. When his department became professional, he became a full-time firefighter, running his
business on the side with the aid of hi s sons, both of whom became firefighters. Mr. Kimura was a
captain when he retired in 1982, and
WHEREAS, Tad J. Kimura further selflessly volunteered his time when he established and for fifty
years was the mainstay of the local blood drive, and
WHEREAS, Tad J. Kimura continued his tireless phi lanthropic endeavors on behalf of his community
when he created the Friday night fish fry at the American Legion to raise funds for Legion charities. The
dinners have been a civic focal point for 44 years drawing 400 people a week, and

2801

 JOURNAL O F PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS, Tad J. Kimura was a man of faith and a charter member of the Buddhist Temple of
Chicago, and
WHEREAS, Tad J. Kimura was honored when he was named Morton Grove's outstanding citizen in
1967, and in 1985 was named " Man of the Year" by the local newspaper. He won numerous awards from
civic groups with which he was actively involved, and
WHEREAS, Tad J. Kimura enhanced the business environment and the lives of the residents of Morton
Grove and left a legacy of devotion to his family, his faith, his country and his community.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does

WHEREAS, Almighty God, in His infinite wisdom, has called Pearlie L. Parks from our midst; and

2803

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001
WHEREAS, born in 1916 in Luverne, Alabama, Pearlie was the sixth child of the late Ada and Ben
Butler; and

WHEREAS, Pearlie attended school in Luverne and soon became a devoted member of the Good Hope
Baptist Church; and

WHEREAS, Pearlie went on to marry C. B. Parks who preceded her in death; their blessed union
produced one daughter, Garrie Parks; Pearlie also had one granddaughter, Pearl Parks; and

WHEREAS, Pearlie also had a special place in her heart for Forrest Little, the one she called son; and

WHEREAS, Pearlie eventually moved to Chicago and quickly found a new religious home with the
Progressive Baptist Church. Pearlie was a dedicated member of the New Rising Sun Missionary Baptist
Church at the time of her homecoming. Pearlie loved God, she loved Sunday school and she loved
church, attending as often as her health would allow; and

WHEREAS, with the passing of Pearlie L. Parks, we have lost a loving mother, grandmother, sister, aunt
and friend who was devoted to her family, gave back to society and positively influenced all with whom
she came in contact. Pearlie exhibited exceptional strength, courage and endurance; she didn't believe in
complaining when things got tough, preferring to simply say " I' ll do my best"; and

WHEREAS, the myriad contributions Pearlie L. Parks made to our world were significant and will
forever resonate.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf of
the more than five million res idents of Cook County, does hereby express its deepest condolences and
most heartfelt sympathy to the many friends and loved ones of Pearlie L. Parks; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the famil y of
Pearlie L. Parks so that her memory may be so honored and ever cherished.

Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

WHEREAS, A lmi ghty God in His infinite w isdom has called from our midst;
HOWARD M. BURGH

2809

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001

WHEREAS, Mr. Burgh spent his lifetime working tirelessly for his county, his family and his
community; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Burgh was born on May 8, 1921 on Chicago's West Side and attended Austin High
School and graduated in the Class of 1939 I /2; and
WHEREAS, upon graduation, during the height of World War II, Mr. Burgh enlisted in the United States
Army and served with valor and bravery in the North Apennines campaign in Italy, during the brutal
world wide conflict. Mr. Burgh was awarded two Bronze Stars and a Purple Heart for his exemplary
conduct, he was injured in action and was returned stateside for recovery; and
WHEREAS, after the war Mr. Burgh arrived back home to Chicago, in 1947 he wed Irene Boller and
together they raised a family of six; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Burgh regularly demonstrated his ability to lead and to come up with innovative ideas
and after working for several years as a salesman for a fluid power products company, he believed he
could run a business more effectively. In 1954, with a fellow employee, he founded Flow Products Inc. in
the City's Northwest Side; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Burgh lead Flow Products Inc. as its President from 1954 until hi s death; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Burgh was a charter member of the Fluid Power Distributors Association, but he was
not only a business leader, he was also a leader in his community. He was a member of the Young
President's Association and the Holy Name Father's Club, Divine Infant Parish in Westchester, Illinois, a
Lifetime Trustee of Fenwick High School in Oak Park, Illinois and a Commander of his American Legion
Post; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Burgh is s urvived by his wife, Irene; their daughters, Mary Ann Sipsma and Christine
Kocher; their sons, Howard Jr., Brian, Gregory and Scott; and seven grandchildren; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Burgh was a beloved and revered man.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Mr. Howard Burgh, and offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
family and friends in their hour of sorrow and joins them in honoring hi s memory ; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Mr. Burgh's
family as a memorial of his good works and spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 200 I.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County C lerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

01-R-558
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ROBERTO MALDONADO, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ, WILLIAM R. MORAN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
MIKE QUIGLEY, HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the Members of the Cook County Board were deeply saddened to learn of the death at age
78 of Theresa Hendrix, one of Chicago's great community activists; and
WHEREAS, the child of Italian immigrants, Theresa Hendrix was raised on the near west side of
Chicago where she later raised her five chil dren, Sam, Thurmond, Bob, Mary and Tom; and
WHEREAS, Mrs. Hendrix attended Wells High School , leaving after her sophomore year to work for
Leaf, Inc., a Chicago candy maker, to help support her six siblings; and
WHEREAS, married in 1943, Theresa was a lifelong companion to Thurman Hendrix, her husband of26
years, and a loving and supportive mother to her children encouraging them to live life to its fullest as she
had always done; and
WHEREAS, for 50 years, Mrs. Hendrix served as PTA president at Talcott Elementary School where all
five of her children had attended, and as the head of the mother's club at Emerson House, a social service
agency; and
WHEREAS, renowned for her generosity and compassion, Theresa Hendrix was a lifeline for many
people in the neighborhood, a lways extending a helping hand to her friends and neighbors; and
WHEREAS, the recipient of many honors and awards, Mrs. Hendrix received a "Sun-Times Jefferson
Award" for community service and the City of Chicago named the 1800 block of West Huron in her
honor; and
WHEREAS, Theresa Hendrix will always be remembered for her sharp wit, her saucy personality, he r
irrepressible spirit, and her inimitable style.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that the
Board does hereby honor the life and memory of Theresa Hendrix and extend our heartfelt condolences to
her fami ly; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a s uitable copy of thi s Resolution be presented to the family of
Theresa Hendrix as a sign of our sympathy and good wishes.

01-R-560
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT AND CARL R. HANSEN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, as a result of the problems encountered in the November 2000 presidential election, the

National Association of Counties (NACo) joined with the National Association of County Recorders,
Election Officials and Clerks, in establishing the National Commi ssion on Election Standards and Reform
(the Commission) comprised of county commissioners and election officials from across the United
States; and
WHEREAS, the Commission focused on problems of voter access, voting systems, recount procedures
and perceptions of partisanship in the operation of the election system and published a report of their
findings and recommendations entitled Report and Recommendation to Improve America's Election
System; and
WH EREAS, NACo's Committee on Finance and Intergovernmental Affairs has by resolution endorsed

the Commission's recommendations and report, particu larly noting that governments at all levels must
ensure and maintain the secrecy of the ballot; and
WHEREAS, the Commission recommendations regarding funding, administration and the conduct of

elections, particularly the need to ensure and maintain the secrecy of the ballot will service the best
interest of the public.

2813

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR AUGUST 9, 2001

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Cook County Commissioners hereby
adopts the NA Co endorsement of the Commission Report.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of August 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to suspend the rules so that
this matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Moran, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
